Mean and\\n755:     standard deviation are then stored to be used on later data using\\n756:     :meth:`transform`.\\n757: \\n758:     Standardization of a dataset is a common requirement for many\\n759:     machine learning estimators: they might behave badly if the\\n760:     individual features do not more or less look like standard normally\\n761:     distributed data (e.g. Gaussian with 0 mean and unit variance).\\n762: \\n763:     For instance many elements used in the objective function of\\n764:     a learning algorithm (such as the RBF kernel of Support Vector\\n765:     Machines or the L1 and L2 regularizers of linear models) assume that\\n766:     all features are centered around 0 and have variance in the same\\n767:     order. If a feature has a variance that is orders of magnitude larger\\n768:     than others, it might dominate the objective function and make the\\n769:     estimator unable to learn from other features correctly as expected.\\n770: \\n771:     `StandardScaler` is sensitive to outliers, and the features may scale\\n772:     differently from each other in the presence of outliers. For an example\\n773:     visualization, refer to :ref:`Compare StandardScaler with other scalers\\n774:     <plot_all_scaling_standard_scaler_section>`.\\n775: \\n776:     This scaler can also be applied to sparse CSR or CSC matrices by passing\\n777:     `with_mean=False` to avoid breaking the sparsity structure of the data.\\n778: \\n779:     Read more in the :ref:`User Guide <preprocessing_scaler>`.\\n780: \\n781:     Parameters\\n782:     ----------\\n783:     copy : bool, default=True\\n784:         If False, try to avoid a copy and do inplace scaling instead.\\n785:         This is not guaranteed to always work inplace; e.g. if the data is\\n786:         not a NumPy array or scipy.sparse CSR matrix, a copy may still be\\n787:         returned.\\n788: \\n789:     with_mean : bool, default=True\\n790:         If True, center the data before scaling.\\n791:         This does not work (and will raise an exception) when attempted on\\n792:         sparse matrices, because centering them entails building a dense\\n793:         matrix which in common use cases is likely to be too large to fit in\\n794:         memory.\\n795: \\n796:     with_std : bool, default=True\\n797:         If True, scale the data to unit variance (or equivalently,\\n798:         unit standard deviation).\\n799: \\n800:     Attributes\\n801:     ----------\\n802:     scale_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n803:         Per feature relative scaling of the data to achieve zero mean and unit\\n804:         variance. Generally this is calculated using `np.sqrt(var_)`. If a\\n805:         variance is zero, we can't achieve unit variance, and the data is left\\n806:         as-is, giving a scaling factor of 1. `scale_` is equal to `None`\\n807:         when `with_std=False`.\\n808: \\n809:         .. versionadded:: 0.17\\n810:            *scale_*\\n811: \\n812:     mean_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n813:         The mean value for each feature in the training set.\\n814:         Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and ``with_std=False``.\\n815: \\n816:     var_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n817:         The variance for each feature in the training set. Used to compute\\n818:         `scale_`. Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and\\n819:         ``with_std=False``.\\n820: \\n821:     n_features_in_ : int\\n822:         Number of features seen during :term:`fit`.\\n823: \\n824:         .. versionadded:: 0.24\\n825: \\n826:     feature_names_in_ : ndarray of shape (`n_features_in_`,)\\n827:         Names of features seen during :term:`fit`. Defined only when `X`\\n828:         has feature names that are all strings.\\n829: \\n830:         .. versionadded:: 1.0\\n831: \\n832:     n_samples_seen_ : int or ndarray of shape (n_features,)\\n833:         The number of samples processed by the estimator for each feature.\\n834:         If there are no missing samples, the ``n_samples_seen`` will be an\\n835:         integer, otherwise it will be an array of dtype int. If\\n836:         `sample_weights` are used it will be a float (if no missing data)\\n837:         or an array of dtype float that sums the weights seen so far.\\n838:         Will be reset on new calls to fit, but increments across\\n839:         ``partial_fit`` calls.\\n840: \\n841:     See Also\\n842:     --------\\n843:     scale : Equivalent function without the estimator API.\\n844: \\n845:     :class:`~sklearn.decomposition.PCA` : Further removes the linear\\n846:         correlation across features with 'whiten=True'.\\n847: \\n848:     Notes\\n849:     -----\\n850:     NaNs are treated as missing values: disregarded in fit, and maintained in\\n851: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/scikit-learn--cb7e82dd@72904752e88f414cbc543dac5945b6c8dd7b34fa/-/blob/sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py%3FL740-850\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a670c6ae-1c04-4aac-a3f6-5760006959d1","uuid":"a96f3733-842f-44e8-bc1f-9a705a26fe24","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"740: class StandardScaler(OneToOneFeatureMixin, TransformerMixin, BaseEstimator):\\n741:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Standardize features by removing the mean and scaling to unit variance.\\n742: \\n743:     The standard score of a sample `x` is calculated as:\\n744: \\n745:     .. code-block:: text\\n746: \\n747:         z = (x - u) / s\\n748: \\n749:     where `u` is the mean of the training samples or zero if `with_mean=False`,\\n750:     and `s` is the standard deviation of the training samples or one if\\n751:     `with_std=False`.\\n752: \\n753:     Centering and scaling happen independently on each feature by computing\\n754:     the relevant statistics on the samples in the training set. If a\\n805:         variance is zero, we can't achieve unit variance, and the data is left\\n806:         as-is, giving a scaling factor of 1. `scale_` is equal to `None`\\n807:         when `with_std=False`.\\n808: \\n809:         .. versionadded:: 0.17\\n810:            *scale_*\\n811: \\n812:     mean_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n813:         The mean value for each feature in the training set.\\n814:         Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and ``with_std=False``.\\n815: \\n816:     var_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n817:         The variance for each feature in the training set. Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and\\n819:         ``with_std=False``.\\n820: \\n821:     n_features_in_ : int\\n822:         Number of features seen during :term:`fit`.\\n823: \\n824:         .. versionadded:: 0.24\\n825: \\n826:     feature_names_in_ : ndarray of shape (`n_features_in_`,)\\n827:         Names of features seen during :term:`fit`. Defined only when `X`\\n828:         has feature names that are all strings.\\n829: \\n830:         .. versionadded:: 1.0\\n831: \\n832:     n_samples_seen_ : int or ndarray of shape (n_features,)\\n833:         The number of samples processed by the estimator for each feature.\\n834:         If there are no missing samples, the ``n_samples_seen`` will be an\\n835:         integer, otherwise it will be an array of dtype int. If\\n836:         `sample_weights` are used it will be a float (if no missing data)\\n837:         or an array of dtype float that sums the weights seen so far.\\n838:         Will be reset on new calls to fit, but increments across\\n839:         ``partial_fit`` calls.\\n840: \\n841:     See Also\\n842:     --------\\n843:     scale : Equivalent function without the estimator API.\\n844: \\n845:     :class:`~sklearn.decomposition.PCA` : Further removes the linear\\n846:         correlation across features with 'whiten=True'.\\n847: \\n848:     Notes\\n849:     -----\\n850:     NaNs are treated as missing values: disregarded in fit, and maintained in\\n851: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/scikit-learn--cb7e82dd@72904752e88f414cbc543dac5945b6c8dd7b34fa/-/blob/sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py%3FL740-850\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"740: class StandardScaler(OneToOneFeatureMixin, TransformerMixin, BaseEstimator):\n741:     \"\"\"Standardize features by removing the mean and scaling to unit variance.\n742: \n743:     The standard score of a sample `x` is calculated as:\n744: \n745:     .. code-block:: text\n746: \n747:         z = (x - u) / s\n748: \n749:     where `u` is the mean of the training samples or zero if `with_mean=False`,\n750:     and `s` is the standard deviation of the training samples or one if\n751:     `with_std=False`.\n752: \n753:     Centering and scaling happen independently on each feature by computing\n754:     the relevant statistics on the samples in the training set. Mean and\n755:     standard deviation are then stored to be used on later data using\n756:     :meth:`transform`.\n757: \n758:     Standardization of a dataset is a common requirement for many\n759:     machine learning estimators: they might behave badly if the\n760:     individual features do not more or less look like standard normally\n761:     distributed data (e.g. Gaussian with 0 mean and unit variance).\n762: \n763:     For instance many elements used in the objective function of\n764:     a learning algorithm (such as the RBF kernel of Support Vector\n765:     Machines or the L1 and L2 regularizers of linear models) assume that\n766:     all features are centered around 0 and have variance in the same\n767:     order. If a feature has a variance that is orders of magnitude larger\n768:     than others, it might dominate the objective function and make the\n769:     estimator unable to learn from other features correctly as expected.\n770: \n771:     `StandardScaler` is sensitive to outliers, and the features may scale\n772:     differently from each other in the presence of outliers. For an example\n773:     visualization, refer to :ref:`Compare StandardScaler with other scalers\n774:     <plot_all_scaling_standard_scaler_section>`.\n775: \n776:     This scaler can also be applied to sparse CSR or CSC matrices by passing\n777:     `with_mean=False` to avoid breaking the sparsity structure of the data.\n778: \n779:     Read more in the :ref:`User Guide <preprocessing_scaler>`.\n780: \n781:     Parameters\n782:     ----------\n783:     copy : bool, default=True\n784:         If False, try to avoid a copy and do inplace scaling instead.\n785:         This is not guaranteed to always work inplace; e.g. if the data is\n786:         not a NumPy array or scipy.sparse CSR matrix, a copy may still be\n787:         returned.\n788: \n789:     with_mean : bool, default=True\n790:         If True, center the data before scaling.\n791:         This does not work (and will raise an exception) when attempted on\n792:         sparse matrices, because centering them entails building a dense\n793:         matrix which in common use cases is likely to be too large to fit in\n794:         memory.\n795: \n796:     with_std : bool, default=True\n797:         If True, scale the data to unit variance (or equivalently,\n798:         unit standard deviation).\n799: \n800:     Attributes\n801:     ----------\n802:     scale_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\n803:         Per feature relative scaling of the data to achieve zero mean and unit\n804:         variance. Generally this is calculated using `np.sqrt(var_)`. If a\n805:         variance is zero, we can't achieve unit variance, and the data is left\n806:         as-is, giving a scaling factor of 1. `scale_` is equal to `None`\n807:         when `with_std=False`.\n808: \n809:         .. versionadded:: 0.17\n810:            *scale_*\n811: \n812:     mean_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\n813:         The mean value for each feature in the training set.\n814:         Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and ``with_std=False``.\n815: \n816:     var_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\n817:         The variance for each feature in the training set. Used to compute\n818:         `scale_`. Equal to ``None`` when ``with_mean=False`` and\n819:         ``with_std=False``.\n820: \n821:     n_features_in_ : int\n822:         Number of features seen during :term:`fit`.\n823: \n824:         .. versionadded:: 0.24\n825: \n826:     feature_names_in_ : ndarray of shape (`n_features_in_`,)\n827:         Names of features seen during :term:`fit`. Defined only when `X`\n828:         has feature names that are all strings.\n829: \n830:         .. versionadded:: 1.0\n831: \n832:     n_samples_seen_ : int or ndarray of shape (n_features,)\n833:         The number of samples processed by the estimator for each feature.\n834:         If there are no missing samples, the ``n_samples_seen`` will be an\n835:         integer, otherwise it will be an array of dtype int. If\n836:         `sample_weights` are used it will be a float (if no missing data)\n837:         or an array of dtype float that sums the weights seen so far.\n838:         Will be reset on new calls to fit, but increments across\n839:         ``partial_fit`` calls.\n840: \n841:     See Also\n842:     --------\n843:     scale : Equivalent function without the estimator API.\n844: \n845:     :class:`~sklearn.decomposition.PCA` : Further removes the linear\n846:         correlation across features with 'whiten=True'.\n847: \n848:     Notes\n849:     -----\n850:     NaNs are treated as missing values: disregarded in fit, and maintained in\n851: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/scikit-learn--cb7e82dd@72904752e88f414cbc543dac5945b6c8dd7b34fa/-/blob/sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py%3FL740-850"}}}

Lines 713-715: INTEGER DTYPES FLAGGED FOR CONVERSION\n    elif is_integer_dtype(pd_dtype):\n        # XXX: Warn when converting from a high integer to a float\n        return True\n\n    return False\n```\n\n**Critical**: Pandas nullable integer types (Int64Dtype, Int32Dtype, etc.) return `True` because `is_integer_dtype()` identifies them as integer types.\n\n#### 2.3 Early Conversion Trigger\n**Location**: Lines 935-942 in `check_array()`\n\n```python\nif pandas_requires_conversion:\n    # pandas dataframe requires conversion earlier to handle extension dtypes with nans\n    # Use the original dtype for conversion if dtype is None\n    new_dtype = dtype_orig if dtype is None else dtype\n    array = array.astype(new_dtype)  # <-- CONVERSION HAPPENS HERE\n    # Since we converted here, we do not need to convert again later\n    dtype = None\n```\n\nWhen `pandas_requires_conversion` is `True`, the code calls `.astype()` on the pandas DataFrame.\n\n### 3. Pandas Masked Array Conversion\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` (lines 694-716)\n\nWhen `.astype()` is called on a DataFrame with nullable integer columns, it triggers the `__array__` interface method:\n\n```python\ndef __array__(\n    self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"the array interface, return my values\"\"\"\n    if copy is False:\n        if not self._hasna:\n            # special case, here we can simply return the underlying data\n            result = np.array(self._data, dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n            return result\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n        )\n\n    if copy is None:\n        copy = False  # The NumPy copy=False meaning is different here.\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)  # <-- CALLS to_numpy()\n```\n\nThis method delegates to `to_numpy()` on line 716.\n\n### 4. Pandas Dtype Inference (ROOT CAUSE)\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` (lines 27-75)\n\nThis is where the critical dtype conversion happens:\n\n```python\ndef to_numpy_dtype_inference(\n    arr: ExtensionArray,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None,\n    na_value,\n    hasna: bool,\n) -> tuple[np.dtype | None, Any]:\n    result_dtype: np.dtype | None\n    inferred_numeric_dtype = False\n    if dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n        inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n        if hasna:\n            if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n            else:\n                # LINES 41-42: THE PROBLEM\n                if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":  # integer or unsigned int\n                    result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # <-- CONVERTS TO FLOAT64!\n                else:\n                    result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n                if na_value is lib.no_default:\n                    if not is_nan_na():\n                        na_value = NA\n                        dtype = np.dtype(object)\n                    else:\n                        na_value = np.nan\n        else:\n            result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n    # ... rest of function\n```\n\n**Root Cause**: Lines 41-42\n\nWhen converting a pandas nullable integer array to a NumPy array:\n1. If the array has missing values (`hasna=True`)\n2. AND the dtype kind is integer (`arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\"`)\n3. The function converts to `np.float64` to accommodate NaN values\n\nThis conversion:\n- **Causes precision loss** for large integers (beyond float64's integer precision threshold of 2^53)\n- **Creates dtype mismatch** with the expected integer dtype\n- **Is incompatible** with NumPy operations expecting integer dtypes\n\n### 5. NumPy Array Processing\n**File**: `numpy/_core/_methods.py`\n\nAfter conversion to float64, NumPy operations may expect integer dtypes for certain operations. The float64 dtype causes issues with:\n- Reductions that expect integers\n- Dtype propagation in statistical functions\n- Compatibility with other NumPy functions\n\n## The Complete Flow\n\n1. **pandas DataFrame with Int64Dtype**\n   ↓\n2. **scikit-learn's validate_data()** detects extension dtype\n   ↓\n3. **_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()** returns True for integer dtypes\n   ↓\n4. **check_array()** calls `.astype()` on the DataFrame\n   ↓\n5. **Pandas masked array's __array__()** delegates to `to_numpy()`\n   ↓\n6. **to_numpy_dtype_inference()** detects missing values\n   ↓\n7. **Integer dtype is converted to float64** (PROBLEM)\n   ↓\n8. **Precision loss and dtype mismatches occur** in downstream NumPy operations\n\n## Files Involved\n\n| Library | File | Line Range | Component |\n|---------|------|-----------|-----------|\n| scikit-learn | `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py` | 961-968 | StandardScaler.partial_fit() |\n| scikit-learn | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 681-717 | _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion() |\n| scikit-learn | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 935-942 | check_array() conversion logic |\n| pandas | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | 694-716 | BaseMaskedArray.__array__() |\n| pandas | `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` | 27-75 | **to_numpy_dtype_inference()** |\n| pandas | `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` | 41-42 | **Integer to float64 conversion** |\n| numpy | `numpy/_core/_methods.py` | (various) | Operations on converted dtypes |\n\n## Root Cause Location\n\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py`\n**Function**: `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`\n**Lines**: 41-42\n\n```python\nif arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":\n    result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)\n```\n\n## Problem Details\n\n### Issue 1: Implicit Integer-to-Float Conversion\nWhen converting pandas nullable integers to NumPy, the library automatically converts them to float64 if missing values are present. This is not transparent to downstream users.\n\n### Issue 2: Precision Loss\nFloat64 can precisely represent integers up to 2^53 (9,007,199,254,740,992). Large integers beyond this threshold lose precision when converted to float64.\n\n### Issue 3: Dtype Mismatch\nDownstream NumPy operations may expect integer dtypes but receive float64 instead, causing:\n- Type errors in operations designed for integers\n- Unexpected behavior in statistical calculations\n- Incompatibility with integer-specific NumPy functions\n\n### Issue 4: Data Loss\nWhen missing values are present:\n- The conversion to float64 is forced\n- The original integer dtype information is lost\n- Recovery of the original integer values is impossible if precision was lost\n\n## Reproduction Scenario\n\n```python\nimport pandas as pd\nimport numpy as np\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n\n# Create DataFrame with nullable integers\ndf = pd.DataFrame({\n    'col1': pd.array([1, 2, 3, pd.NA, 5], dtype='Int64'),\n    'col2': pd.array([10, 20, 30, 40, pd.NA], dtype='Int64')\n})\n\n# Pass to StandardScaler\nscaler = StandardScaler()\nscaler.fit(df)  # Internally calls validate_data()\n\n# At this point:\n# 1. pandas masks detect missing values (pd.NA)\n# 2. to_numpy_dtype_inference converts Int64 -> float64\n# 3.
